					Here is a tautly paced investigation of one the 20th century's most audacious art frauds, which generated hundreds of forgeries - many of them still hanging in prominent museums and private collections today. <i>Provenance</i> is the extraordinary narrative of one of the most far-reaching and elaborate deceptions in art history.

        <p>Close up look at the evolution of the recorded business over the past 30 or so years.  Lots of great detail on personalities, as well as interesting events.  I've been listening to Audible for 14 years, and the narration performed by Dennis Boutsikaris was, by far, the best reading I've ever heard.  The content was 5 star.  The narration was 7 star.</p>

				<p>
					In this star-studded autobiography, Clive Davis shares a personal, candid look into his remarkable life and the last 50 years of popular music as only a true insider can. In the history of popular music, no one looms as large as Clive Davis. His career has spanned more than 40 years, and he has discovered, signed, or worked with a staggering array of artists: Whitney Houston, Janis Joplin, Simon and Garfunkel, Barry Manilow, Patti Smith, Lou Reed, Dionne Warwick, Carlos Santana, The Grateful Dead, Alicia Keyes, Kelly Clarkson, Jennifer Hudson, and Aretha Franklin, to name a few.

					<h3>The Dialogue: An Interview with Screenwriter Simon Kinberg</h3>
				
				<ul>
					<li>

				<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">

				</div>
				<p>
					Simon Kinberg recently burst onto the scene with his script for <i>xXx: State of the Union</i>, and has since worked on comic-to-film adaptations for <i>Elektra</i> and <i>Fantastic Four</i> and penned the third film in the X-Men series, <i>X-Men: The Last Stand</i>. Kinberg's breakthrough hit, <i>Mr. and Mrs. Smith</i>, began as a script that he wrote in college and became one of the top grossing movies of 2005.
				</p>

	<span class="userTile-memberSince">

		<p class="userTile-memberMsg">Computer Programmer and Worship Leader.  Have enjoyed reading since my mom got me hooked on Nancy Drew and Agatha Christie prior to my teen years.  My brother got me hooked on audio books after I started having a longer commute to work.

Love a variety of genres.</p>

		<ul class="adbl-promotedReviews scrollable-items">
			<li class="adbl-promotedReview">
				



















	



	
	
		
		
		
	


<div class="promotedProductReview adbl-flyout-cont-marker">
	

	
	



















    
    
        
        
            
        
    
	








<div class="adbl-prod-image-sample-cont  adbl-full-image">
	<a href="/pd/ref=cat_rev_2226646011?asin=B004GMJ81U">
		
			
			
				<img class="adbl-prod-image" src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/513XsauqgCL._SL95_.jpg" alt="How Music Works: The Science and Psychology of Beautiful Sounds, from Beethoven to the Beatles and Beyond"/>
			
		
		<span class="icon-cornerCurl"></span>
		<span class="icon-daily-deal"></span>
	</a>
	
	
</div>
	
	
	<div class="review-summary" style="position: relative;">
		<h3>"Nearly everyone will get something ..."</h3>
		
		
			<div class="adbl-review-helpfulness">
				3 of 
				3 helpful votes
			</div>
		
		
		<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">
			
			
				
				
					<div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div>
				
			
		</div>
		<div class="review-text">
			





    
        <p>As a guitarist, choral director and musician of over 30 years, I have a pretty good understanding of the physics of music as well as music theory.  However, I came away learning a number of new things from this book AND with a more solid understanding of things I already knew.<br /><br />While I agree that a British reader may have made the listen a little more fun, the narrator was fine for me.  The author's recordings at the end of chapters were good in most cases, but his demonstration of vibrato and rubato were generally not that obvious, even to someone who knew exactly what he was doing and trying to communicate.<br /><br />His explanation of the overtone series and how they contribute to an instrument's sound was VERY good, as was his explanation of how the pentatonic scales were mathematically derived (something that I didn't know).  <br /><br />The author also did a good job near the end of the book explaining the weird "names" for classical compositions.  His appendix explaining the intervals and songs that used them was also very good.<br /><br />Only other criticism (and it is a small one) is that the use of terms tone and semi-tone is less common than whole step and half step, which may confuse some readers a bit.<br /><br />All in all a really nice read and the author has a GREAT sense of humor!</p>
    
    

		</div>
	</div>
	
	
	
		
	
	
		
	<a href="/review-by-author/ref=cat_rev_2226646011_prfl?customerID=AUZK7DROI4PAE&asin=B004GMJ81U" class="adbl-link">More</a>

					<h3>How Music Works: The Science and Psychology of Beautiful Sounds, from Beethoven to the Beatles and Beyond</h3>
				
				<ul>
					<li>
						






UNABRIDGED (8 hrs and 6 mins)
					</li>
					
						<li>By <strong>John Powell</strong>
						</li>
					
					
						<li>Narrated By <strong>Walter Dixon</strong>
						</li>
					
                    <li><div class='adbl-wfs-icon adbl-wfs-text'><div class="adbl-wfs-capable-text">Whispersync for Voice-ready</div></div></li>

				<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">
					<div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Overall</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(146)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Performance</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(106)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Story</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(102)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div>
				</div>
				<p>
					Have you ever wondered how off-key you are while singing in the shower? Or if your Bob Dylan albums really sound better on vinyl? Or why certain songs make you cry? Now, scientist and musician John Powell invites you on an entertaining journey through the world of music. Discover what distinguishes music from plain old noise, how scales help you memorize songs, what the humble recorder teaches you about timbre (assuming your suffering listeners don’t break it first), and more.
				</p>

				<p>
					Jackson, Mississippi, 1962. Aibileen is a black maid raising her 17th white child. Minny, Aibileen's best friend, is the sassiest woman in Mississippi: a wonderful cook with a gossip's tongue. Graduate Skeeter returns from college with ambitions, but her mother will not be happy until she's married. Although world's apart, Skeeter, Aibileen and Minny's lives converge over a clandestine project that will change the town of Jackson forever.

				<p>
					This no-holds-barred autobiography chronicles the remarkable life of Phil Robertson, the original <i>Duck Commander</i> and <i>Duck Dynasty</i> star, from early childhood through the founding of a family business. Life was always getting in the way of Phil Robertson’s passion for duck hunting. An NFL-bound quarterback, Phil made his mark on Louisiana Tech University in the 1960s by playing football and completing his college career with a master’s degree in English. But Phil’s eyes were not always on the books or the ball; they were usually looking to the sky....

					It’s all about the food…. For the Robertsons, family is typified by the dinner table, where both food and fables are dished up with equal care. And that’s what this family is all about - sharing, caring for one another, and the love of good food. Chapters are built around recipes that represent each stage of the Robertson life. What do faith, family, ducks, and money have in common? Korie and Willie Robertson!

					<div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Overall</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(2186)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Performance</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(1053)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Story</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(1043)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div>

				<p>
					Now at last Keith Richards pauses to tell his story in the most anticipated autobiography in decades. And what a story! Listening obsessively to Chuck Berry and Muddy Waters records in a coldwater flat with Mick Jagger and Brian Jones, building a sound and a band out of music they loved. Finding fame and success as a bad-boy band, only to find themselves challenged by authorities everywhere....

					<h3>The 30 Greatest Orchestral Works</h3>
				
				<ul>
					<li>
						






ORIGINAL (24 hrs and 52 mins)
					</li>
					
						<li>By <strong>The Great Courses</strong>
						</li>
					
					
						<li>Narrated By <strong>Professor Robert Greenberg</strong>
						</li>
					
                    <li></li>
				</ul>
				<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">
					<div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Overall</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(8)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-half"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Performance</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(7)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Story</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(8)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-full"></a><a class="adbl-rating-half"></a></div></div>
				</div>
				<p>
					Over the centuries, orchestral music has given us a category of works that stand apart as transcendent expressions of the human spirit. What are these "greatest of the greats"? Find out in these 32 richly detailed lectures that take you on a sumptuous grand tour of the symphonic pieces that continue to live at the center of our musical culture.These 30 masterworks form an essential foundation for any music collection and a focal point for understanding the orchestral medium and deepening your insight into the communicative power of music.
				</p>

					The zombie plague unleashes its horrors on the suburbs of Atlanta without warning, pitting the living against the dead. Dogged by their feral hunger for flesh and crippled by fear, Lilly relies on the protection of good Samaritans by seeking refuge in a walled-in town once known as Woodbury, Georgia. But Lilly begins to suspect that all is not as it seems....

				<p>
					The high-water mark of punk was at the height of a summer of royal love. Millions attended street parties to celebrate the Queen's 25th anniversary on the throne. Meanwhile, a more irreverent party had been planned. A boat laden with The Sex Pistols, their Svengali manager Malcolm McLaren, journalists, and various friends and hangers-on sailed by The Houses of Parliament while The Pistols blasted out Anarchy In The UK. Shortly after, the boat was boarded by police and "persuaded" to return to shore.
				</p>
			</div>

				<p>
					Amy Winehouse is a tragic and extreme example of the price of fame in the UK in the Noughties. She was someone who'd been pursuing fame since childhood. She'd attended theatre schools, learned guitar, and sung with the National Jazz Youth Orchestra. Amy took much or her style from the '60s girl groups (the beehive) and from Ronnie Spector (the Cleopatra eye-liner). Amy's style was somehow already familiar but very fresh to a young audience. With frightening regularity she was on the tabloid's front-pages: Amy with a new tattoo...stumbling from a club...looking skeletal.

				<p>
					This was Britain's first gentle whiff of drug culture in pop music. The sounds of what later became known as the Summer of Love, were first encapsulated on this side of the Atlantic by Procol Harum's hit. The concepts of free love, liberal politics, casual drug use, communal living, and opposition to the Vietnam War were at its core. Slowly the culture had infiltrated first the American West Coast music scene and then more popular culture. In London, everything was just groovy. Hair was worn a little longer, beads were sported, and flowers waved about. "A Whiter Shade of Pale" was the debut single from Procol Harum, which went to number one in the UK.

				<p>
					Afro-Caribbean calypsos had taken root in the folk scene of the early '60s, but for many Britons their first experience of this new music came courtesy of an effervescent, feisty young woman from the Jamaican slums called Millie. "My Boy Lollipop" became the first hit single for Island records. Millie even appeared on a Beatles TV special in 1964. This was the start of a cross cultural pollination.

					<h3>In Spite of Myself</h3>
				
				<ul>
					<li>
						






ABRIDGED (16 hrs and 38 mins)
					</li>
					
						<li>By <strong>Christopher Plummer</strong>
						</li>
					
					
						<li>Narrated By <strong>Christopher Plummer</strong>
						</li>
					
                    <li></li>
				</ul>
				<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">
					<div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Overall</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Performance</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Story</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div>
				</div>
				<p>
					He was born a Canadian on a Friday the 13th in 1929 - the year of the Crash. His boyhood was one of privilege: an ancestor was a Governor General; his great-grandfather Sir John Abbott was Canada’s third prime minister and owned railroads. There were steam yachts, mansions, and a life of Victorian gentility and somewhat cluttered splendor. Plummer tells how "this young bilingual wastrel, incurably romantic, spoiled rotten, tore himself away from the ski slopes to break into the big bad world of theatre, not from the streets up but from an Edwardian living room down".
				</p>
			</div>

					<h3>Hello, Gorgeous: Becoming Barbra Streisand</h3>
				
				<ul>
					<li>
						






UNABRIDGED (20 hrs and 39 mins)
					</li>
					
						<li>By <strong>William J. Mann</strong>
						</li>
					
					
						<li>Narrated By <strong>Elizabeth Morton</strong>
						</li>
					
                    <li></li>
				</ul>
				<div class="adbl-new-stars adbl-new-stars-columns clearfix">
					<div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Overall</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Performance</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div><div class="adbl-rating-wrap clearfix"><div class="adbl-rating-label">Story</div><div class='adbl-rating-num'>(0)</div><div class="adbl-rating-cont adbl-new-stars "><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a><a class="adbl-rating-empty-inactive"></a></div></div>
				</div>
				<p>
					In 1960, she was a 17-year-old Brooklyn kid with plenty of talent but no connections and certainly no money; her mother brought her soup to make sure she stayed fed as she took acting classes and scraped out a living. Just four years later, Barbra Streisand was the top-selling female recording artist in America and the star of one of Broadway’s biggest hits. Now the acclaimed Hollywood biographer William Mann chronicles that dizzying ascent, telling the riveting behind-the-scenes story of how Streisand and her team transformed her from an unknown dreamer into a worldwide superstar.
				</p>
			</div>
			
		</div>
	</div>

        
    
</div>

					</li>
				
			</ul>
